  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a15e6f07-51e3-487c-8466-933563376e04'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023287021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer503484204814992065"><b>3.5 "Vanilla" Stars</b><br/><br/>I didn’t read the blurb, I didn’t read any reviews, I just saw the cover and then added it! I said it so you know how I like the cover!<br/><br/>Okay, now about the story! I enjoyed it but it was far from what I expected. I thought it is BDSM but nope! I mean yes, Calloway has a BDSM club but the story itself hadn’t anything like that. It was slow so I think the BDSM part will come in the next installment. I liked Rome so much. She is confident, feisty and bada$$. She runs a small nonpr</span>
  <span id="freeText503484204814992065" style="display:none"><b>3.5 "Vanilla" Stars</b><br /><br />I didn’t read the blurb, I didn’t read any reviews, I just saw the cover and then added it! I said it so you know how I like the cover!<br /><br />Okay, now about the story! I enjoyed it but it was far from what I expected. I thought it is BDSM but nope! I mean yes, Calloway has a BDSM club but the story itself hadn’t anything like that. It was slow so I think the BDSM part will come in the next installment. I liked Rome so much. She is confident, feisty and bada$$. She runs a small nonprofit. She doesn’t listen to Cal direct orders. Cal is a control freak. He wants to be in control so you can imagine her resistance how affected him but he always found a way to win. But the main problem is whether Cal can live vanilla way or not something we don't know unless we read the next book! So I think this book was something like introductory (to meet with characters and know more about them).<br /><br />The story is told in dual POV, 1st person. it’s the first installment in "Obsidian" series. It ends with a cliffhanger but not a huge one and I definitely would read the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="503484204814992065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer8441157771210177443"><strong>Strength Within</strong><br/><br/>This book is a good read. I enjoy how the story unfolds.<br/><br/>I did not give this five stars even though I liked it, here is why. While very well written I find the story to be a watered down version of Fifty Shades. I was expect to ng more fr</span>
  <span id="freeText8441157771210177443" style="display:none"><strong>Strength Within</strong><br /><br />This book is a good read. I liked the storyline and the struggles Cal faces in his earnest longing for a women that is contrary to everything he thinks he wants. Rome is the personification of an independent woman a role she struggles to maintain as she falls for Calloway. I enjoy how the story unfolds.<br /><br />I did not give this five stars even though I liked it, here is why. While very well written I find the story to be a watered down version of Fifty Shades. I was expect to ng more from the advertisements, however, did not receive it. I also do not like how the story just ended. This is definitely a series that does not stand alone.<br /><br />Altogether, this was a good book. I do not know if I am willing to read the remaining books in the series. We will see.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8441157771210177443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Martin- Loudermilk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Martin- Loudermilk" href="/user/show/57035664-kelly-martin--loudermilk">Kelly Martin- Loudermilk</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2497029528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13810587896869732353">I got this for $1.99 on one of Amazon's Kindle Daily Deals; it didn't disppoint me. I've already bought book 2.<br/><br/>The story has one great hook right at the beginning. Rome (the main female character) is in a bar with a friend and the friend noticies a gentleman at the bar. It's the guy that is married and is cheating on his wife. So, Rome goes right up to the guy and slaps him at the bar. The problem is that Rome slaps the wrong guy--she slaps Calloway instead of the married low life that is cheati</span>
  <span id="freeText13810587896869732353" style="display:none">I got this for $1.99 on one of Amazon's Kindle Daily Deals; it didn't disppoint me. I've already bought book 2.<br /><br />The story has one great hook right at the beginning. Rome (the main female character) is in a bar with a friend and the friend noticies a gentleman at the bar. It's the guy that is married and is cheating on his wife. So, Rome goes right up to the guy and slaps him at the bar. The problem is that Rome slaps the wrong guy--she slaps Calloway instead of the married low life that is cheating on his wife.<br /><br />Calloway runs a non-profit and Rome also runs a non-profit. Rome is a fiesty girl and she's strong and independent and doesn't want anyone to "take care of her". Call it pride, call it strength, whatever you call it...she's got guts. She is who she is.<br /><br />Calloway likes control and he likes being the guy in charge so when Rome slaps him not only does it catch him off guard but it piques his interest. He becomes so intrigued by this girl. He even hires someone to tell him more information but doesn't find anything.<br /><br />This is where the book is different but so much better than 50 Shades of Grey. Calloway takes his time getting to know Rome and Rome does the same thing with Calloway. There's not any BDSM. They are truly establishing their relationship and taking things slow. It's definately a better version of a romance that features a smidge of other stuff, but I would say this is 90% romance. I did like that Calloway wasn't really much of a "stalker" like Christian Grey was. It was just so much better. Also, Rome didn't want to even move in with Calloway. She wanted to establish herself in her own right and that is what really made me enjoy this novel more.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13810587896869732353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1937598893?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy" href="/user/show/12062530-cathy">Cathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1937598893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17550581286976017150">This book felt a lot like 50 Shades of Grey, and yet I feel the writing is so much better. I LOVED Rome's independence and stubbornness, she didn't just give in to Calloway. He is a Dom and yet he would do whatever to win her over as he thinks he can make her his sub. Both have a rough past,, and it is nice to see bits and pieces of that past throughout the book. <br/><br/>This book itself I wouldn't say is dark, but maybe they get darker as the series continues.<br/><br/>Both Calloway and Rome work for non-profits</span>
  <span id="freeText17550581286976017150" style="display:none">This book felt a lot like 50 Shades of Grey, and yet I feel the writing is so much better. I LOVED Rome's independence and stubbornness, she didn't just give in to Calloway. He is a Dom and yet he would do whatever to win her over as he thinks he can make her his sub. Both have a rough past,, and it is nice to see bits and pieces of that past throughout the book. <br /><br />This book itself I wouldn't say is dark, but maybe they get darker as the series continues.<br /><br />Both Calloway and Rome work for non-profits and I love seeing them giving back to others in this book, Rome is barely getting by and of course Cal is a billionaire. <br /><br />The writing is fantastic and again I love the stubbornness and independence of Rome and I hope that never changes. A part of me hopes she never submits as his sub, because I really feel like part of what he likes about her so much is that she stands her ground and doesn't just give in to his every demand.<br /><br />The way they met is the BEST. And of course he was turned on by her slapping him several times. It was refreshing to see her make a fool of herself a few times early on, it makes her a more realistic character. I can't wait to see where this series goes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17550581286976017150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

She's the kind of heroine you will love...She's a pretty little thing, fierce, intelligent, kind, altruist but still so innocent.<br/><br/>Calloway is an intresting hero, he's sexy, dominating and controlling and he hides a pain</span>
  <span id="freeText15073818524606546899" style="display:none"><b>Loved it!! </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492255820i/22498441._SY540_.png" width="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you loved Fifty Shades, you will love this one too, because the books have many similarities.<br><br>I loved Rome, so much. She's so fierce &amp; has achieved so much by herself. Loved how altruist &amp; dedicated to others she is, and can't wait to read more about her hurtful past. She's the kind of heroine you will love...She's a pretty little thing, fierce, intelligent, kind, altruist but still so innocent.<br><br>Calloway is an intresting hero, he's sexy, dominating and controlling and he hides a painful past too.<br><br>I loved how their story began with her mistaking him for someone else and slaping him 3 times, him enjoying it too much. How Cal wanted to make her his sub but ended in a dry spell for 1 month and now he's enjoying Vanilla too much...lol<br><br>I recommend this book, if you want to read something with Fifty Shades flavor.<br><br>Book 1 doesn't end with a cliffhanger.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1934079939" />
    <a title="Melinda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14798785-melinda"><img alt="Melinda" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1934079939?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda" href="/user/show/14798785-melinda">Melinda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1934079939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4361194772816406923">When I received an email about this book from a favorite author, I knew that I would enjoy it and maybe even love it. I timed my reading just right so that I could give this book my undivided attention on the weekend. <br/><br/>It exceeded all my expectations and I am so glad that I stretched it out (started Friday and just finished it tonight, Tuesday) and savored it bit by bit. I've fallen in love with the characters and isn't really accomplished! <br/><br/>The story starts off in a bar with a case of mistaken id</span>
  <span id="freeText4361194772816406923" style="display:none">When I received an email about this book from a favorite author, I knew that I would enjoy it and maybe even love it. I timed my reading just right so that I could give this book my undivided attention on the weekend. <br /><br />It exceeded all my expectations and I am so glad that I stretched it out (started Friday and just finished it tonight, Tuesday) and savored it bit by bit. I've fallen in love with the characters and isn't really accomplished! <br /><br />The story starts off in a bar with a case of mistaken identity when Rome Moretti stands up for her friend and slaps the wrong guy, thinking he cheated on his wife with her bestie. The guy is a Dominant who is quickly turned on by this strong, beautiful, courageous woman and immediately decides that he wants her as his submissive and breaks off his year long relationship with his current sub so that he can pursue (and win) Rome. Calloway agrees to take things slow so the two of them can get to know each other (steamy with everything BUT intercourse) over a period of several weeks. <br /><br />Rome doesn't know it, but Calloway is pursuing her as the ultimate submissive. This proves difficult as Rome is anything but submissive and Calloway is keeping his darker, controlling, dominant side at bay as their relationship continues to build and grow into something special. They each come from troubled pasts and Rome is cautiously thrilled to have finally met her match. He is just as giving as she is when it comes to humanitarian work and she feels he may be just as broken (yet just as strong) as she is. <br /><br />The attraction (and love?) that they have grows quickly even as Calloway continues to subdue his dominate personality while Rome continues to fall for him and allows him to care/protect her. <br /> <br />I loved this book and after a couple chapters, found myself quickly turning the pages and getting sucked into their world. This is by far the best book that I've read in a very long time ands I can't wait to read the next book. I believe the next one is coming out in June so I've marked my calendar and cannot WAIT to read it. <br /><br />Lastly, I would like to say thank you to the author, Victoria Quinn, for taking the time to write a truly great story and I look forward to many more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4361194772816406923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2079018-kristy-mills?shelf=alpha-hotness">alpha-hotness</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3058142220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10317016213549195378">Hmmm so this just sort of ends. I’m not a huge fan of cliffhangers unless it’s a series like this. I felt like the ending needed that little push. It needed something major to happen to make me say “oh snap!” And want to read the next book.<br/><br/>I think I would have enjoyed this book so much more if it weren’t for the narrators. They aren’t terrible or have any annoying habits. But the guy sometimes comes off sounding a little creepy. And the female I just annoyed me with the way she said things somet</span>
  <span id="freeText10317016213549195378" style="display:none">Hmmm so this just sort of ends. I’m not a huge fan of cliffhangers unless it’s a series like this. I felt like the ending needed that little push. It needed something major to happen to make me say “oh snap!” And want to read the next book.<br /><br />I think I would have enjoyed this book so much more if it weren’t for the narrators. They aren’t terrible or have any annoying habits. But the guy sometimes comes off sounding a little creepy. And the female I just annoyed me with the way she said things sometimes. Which made me feel annoyance with the character, all because of a certain inflection or emotion the narrator used.<br /><br />Anyway, Calloway is a Dom. He sees Rome in a bar and immediately knows he wants her. So he breaks off his year long Dom/sub relationship to pursue Rome. Rome is a good girl and he hides his Dom lifestyle from her. But he can’t hide it all the time. His dominant side won’t stay hidden and he has outbursts m. But instead of feeling scared or threatened, Rome responds, and sort of likes it. But she never admits it out loud. <br /><br />Side note: It kind of annoyed me that she starts responding and getting excited by his Dom side, because I was looking for a book where the H is into a Dom/sub lifestyle and the h absolutely does not want anything to do with it. And this was what was recommended to me. So I hope it doesn’t end up with her on her knees.<br /><br />Overall, this was good. I felt like the book just ends though. There is no real climax. It just ends, and the next book picks up immediately where the story left off. I wish something would have happened at the end to shock me. I’m ready for something to happen.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10317016213549195378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10568761242542273419" style="display:none">I liked the heroine in this -- she was tough and opinionated -- and the hero was okay. What bothered me most about it was the language. Sometimes it was just too crass -- almost porn sounding. I love smut, so don't get me wrong. But I like romantic smut. And I like smut with chemistry. These two people didn't have much of either through most of the book. She makes him wait for a few months before they have sex -- well, intercourse. They actually do "have sex." He's a dominant and in between submissives. He hopes she -- a vanilla -- will eventually learn to become his submissive. In the meantime, he's falling in love with her, although he is in denial about it. He's the one who sounds perfunctory about sex, which he should as he sees it as recreational and a physical release, but when he thinks that way about the heroine all the time, it is jarring. I might eventually listen to the next one in this series, but not now. I'm just not that into it. The narrators for this audio book were good, but I did like Lia Langola much better than Michael Ferraiuolo. Michael's voice grated after a while and I didn't care for his female voice.</span>

  <span id="freeText6184412702108995123" style="display:none">Is it possible for a DOM to fall in love at first sight? With a Vanilla girl? Fifty Shades move over! Calloway and Rome are here!<br /><br />She took his breath away from the very instant she entered the room. She became his obsession and once he spent time with her, he was unable to walk away. He wanted her submission and her acquiescence. He was willing to turn his upside down just for the chance to teach her his ways.<br />Seduction is at its best in this story. It sensual and passionate but it is the anticipation of their first sexual encounter that will have you panting for more.<br /><br />I have never read anything by this author, but she has a fan now. I can hardly wait to read the next book in this series to find out what happens next.<br /><br />I am leaving this review on a voluntary basis. Thank you to the author for a copy of her book.</span>

<div id="review_2733449352" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2733449352" />
    <a title="Julian Arce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15558501-julian-arce"><img alt="Julian Arce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355752490p2/15558501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2733449352?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julian Arce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julian Arce" href="/user/show/15558501-julian-arce">Julian Arce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2733449352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer696569726249996141">I read this book because Amazon was giving it away for free... it is complicated.<br/><br/>For starters, I think that it presents in a very negative light the BDSM community; they are portrayed as strange, alien, dangerous. The sub-dom behaviours are carried to all spheres of their lives, whereas for real people is usually only a sexual behavior. Also, I find it strange that all sub-dom relationships are female-male, but in the real world people take different roles according to preferensce. And finally <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(</a></span>
  <span id="freeText696569726249996141" style="display:none">I read this book because Amazon was giving it away for free... it is complicated.<br /><br />For starters, I think that it presents in a very negative light the BDSM community; they are portrayed as strange, alien, dangerous. The sub-dom behaviours are carried to all spheres of their lives, whereas for real people is usually only a sexual behavior. Also, I find it strange that all sub-dom relationships are female-male, but in the real world people take different roles according to preferensce. And finally <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ it bothers me that Cal, the dom in the book is portrayed as a deeply scarred and psychologically unstable person, almost as if people into BDSM are expressing some emotional scars  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Second, the characters make no sense whatsoever. Their public personas are so divorced to their inner monologues and motivations, to the point that they come as schizophrenic. Cal personal lifestyle choices are too far awy from his "job" and day activities, so much so that they actually seem like a plot device. Rome is a strong independent woman... but incredibly volluble to her desires, and it bothers me the degree to which she relies on her brother. And the brother is simply a scumbag <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I mean, he has two important moments in the book, in one he is used to normalize and convince Rome that Cal's aggresive behavior is normal, and then he outright lies and tricks his sister just to get a nice new apartment? Brother of the year  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Third, during the whole book there is a strange tension, since Cal is in theory trying to break Rome into being his sub... but also not really doing it? Chapter to chapter his narration does huge jumps, in one moment he is almost twirling his moustache evil-style about what he is going to do this woman, and in the next he is opening his soul, sharing secrets that no one else knows... it would be something if the inconsistency related to the POV (since we switch between Cal and Rome), but it is not. Many times I thought that book finally was going to go on either direction, but alas, no <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Yes, Cal does admit to himself in the literal last words of the book that he fears that she is changing him... but too little, too late, and to disjointed  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Fourth, it is an erotic book so the sex scenes are of course part of the appeal. And while they are reasonably well constructed... I have several issues such as: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ For a sub-dom book the sex scenes are incredibly vanilla... if the idea is to present a hot BDSM fantasy, why we stop at "fooling around" for most of the book? Cal almost couldn't take it, and neither could I. I also find... strange for lack of a better world the whole viriginity aspect of the book. For starters it is stupid to reduce sex to penetration - I found no part of the book that said that Rome didn't had other partners where she presumably "fooled around" and developed as a sexual person... why is the act of penetration and vaginal sex so important and almost magical. It is so naive. It also has this subtext of "waiting for the right one" that has done so much harm for women, and I just can't abide by it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And finally, I fear that, not the book itself but the series as a whole, is trying to set a grand "redemption" arc where Rome is going to save Cal from his tortured past and wicked ways, and bring him into the light. That would be sad - to equate sexual preferences to something that needs to be fixed, as well as the idea that "love" or "relationships" can save you... On the other hand if Cal does "break" Rome, then it is basically a tragedy. So I find no safe port where this series could be headed. Of course I write this with no knowledge of the rest of the books, so who knows. I wont, because I'm not spending a dime in the series.<br /><br />I guess it was technically well written (or at least passable) and there is a real spice in the sex scenes, hence the 2 starts instead of 1.</span>
  <a data-text-id="696569726249996141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZC6tbT8emQJ0RN9CsyK1/CfzKzjNJ93HXHPTHUXFqf60N9VZ79rDKLxGngbzoZwU+00+C4woLzCxTa2Q+mvpTQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sNXw7hRxZTbIEwW3/BuXIEEYXOoTN5zfIuTyOWwWHVJgzIjaxLU/HAARRPO8mL7InaZJ2VI4bijP2oy007hd4Q==')})
  }

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
